###begin article-title 0
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 15 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Scn3b knockout mice exhibit abnormal ventricular electrophysiological properties
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Both authors contributed equally to this work.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
This document may be redistributed and reused, subject to .
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Abstract
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 135 140 135 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 147 152 147 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 152 155 152 155 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 158 163 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 163 166 163 166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 274 279 274 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 364 369 364 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 369 372 369 372 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 437 442 437 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 471 476 471 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 541 546 541 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 551 556 551 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 642 647 642 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 647 650 647 650 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 773 778 773 778 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 778 781 778 781 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 950 951 950 951 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 953 954 953 954 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1214 1219 1214 1219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1219 1222 1219 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1245 1247 1241 1243 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1389 1394 1385 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1394 1397 1390 1393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1433 1434 1429 1430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1613 1618 1609 1614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1731 1736 1727 1732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1736 1739 1732 1735 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 110 116 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 167 171 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We report for the first time abnormalities in cardiac ventricular electrophysiology in a genetically modified murine model lacking the Scn3b gene (Scn3b-/-). Scn3b-/- mice were created by homologous recombination in embryonic stem (ES) cells. RT-PCR analysis confirmed that Scn3b mRNA was expressed in the ventricles of wild-type (WT) hearts but was absent in the Scn3b-/- hearts. These hearts also showed increased expression levels of Scn1b mRNA in both ventricles and Scn5a mRNA in the right ventricles compared to findings in WT hearts. Scn1b and Scn5a mRNA was expressed at higher levels in the left than in the right ventricles of both Scn3b-/- and WT hearts. Bipolar electrogram and monophasic action potential recordings from the ventricles of Langendorff-perfused Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated significantly shorter ventricular effective refractory periods (VERPs), larger ratios of electrogram duration obtained at the shortest and longest S1-S2 intervals, and ventricular tachycardias (VTs) induced by programmed electrical stimulation. Such arrhythmogenesis took the form of either monomorphic or polymorphic VT. Despite shorter action potential durations (APDs) in both the endocardium and epicardium, Scn3b-/- hearts showed DeltaAPD90 values that remained similar to those shown in WT hearts. The whole-cell patch-clamp technique applied to ventricular myocytes isolated from Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated reduced peak Na+ current densities and inactivation curves that were shifted in the negative direction, relative to those shown in WT myocytes. Together, these findings associate the lack of the Scn3b gene with arrhythmic tendencies in intact perfused hearts and electrophysiological features similar to those in Scn5a+/- hearts.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Keywords
###end title 5
###begin title 6
Introduction
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 24 25 24 25 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 84 113 84 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib22" ref-type="bibr">Keating and Sanguinetti, 2001</xref>
###xml 143 148 143 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 174 178 170 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 189 199 182 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib17" ref-type="bibr">Isom, 2001</xref>
###xml 255 262 248 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xenopus</italic>
###xml 293 298 286 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 336 337 325 326 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 348 365 337 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib36" ref-type="bibr">Noda et&#160;al., 1986</xref>
###xml 382 387 371 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 400 401 385 386 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 407 408 392 393 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 509 514 494 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN5A</italic>
###xml 545 550 530 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 562 563 543 544 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 662 678 643 659 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib47" ref-type="bibr">Tan et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 255 262 <span type="species:ncbi:8355">Xenopus</span>
Voltage-gated sodium (Na+) channels, critical for the excitation of cardiac muscle (Keating and Sanguinetti, 2001), are formed of pore-forming alpha-subunits and one or more beta-subunits (Isom, 2001). Experiments using the two-electrode voltage clamp in Xenopus oocytes demonstrated that the alpha-subunits alone can form functional Na+ channels (Noda et al., 1986). Thus far nine alpha-subunits, Nav1.1-Nav1.9 are each encoded by different genes and have been identified and cloned in mammals. Mutations in SCN5A which encodes for the cardiac alpha-subunit, Nav1.5, can result in arrhythmic conditions, including the Brugada (BrS) and Long QT syndrome (LQTS) (Tan et al., 2003).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 43 47 43 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 86 87 83 84 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 127 131 124 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 200 205 194 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN1B</italic>
###xml 207 212 201 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN2B</italic>
###xml 214 219 208 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN3B</italic>
###xml 224 229 218 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN4B</italic>
###xml 231 341 225 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib18 bib19 bib21 bib35 bib40 bib54" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1992, 1995a; Kazen-Gillespie et&#160;al., 2000; Morgan et&#160;al., 2000; Qin et&#160;al., 2003; Yu et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 374 378 368 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 378 379 369 370 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 381 385 372 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 385 386 373 374 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 388 392 376 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 392 393 377 378 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 398 402 383 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 402 403 384 385 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 510 553 492 535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib5 bib44" ref-type="bibr">Candenas et&#160;al., 2006; Stevens et&#160;al., 2001</xref>
###xml 570 574 552 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 574 575 553 554 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 580 584 559 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 584 585 560 561 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 649 653 625 626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 653 654 626 627 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 659 663 632 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 663 664 633 634 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 732 750 702 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib29" ref-type="bibr">Maier et&#160;al., 2004</xref>
###xml 444 449 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 703 709 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
However, the electrophysiological roles of beta-subunits in the function of cardiac Na+ channels are less well understood. Six beta-subunits have been identified and are encoded by 4 different genes; SCN1B, SCN2B, SCN3B and SCN4B (Isom et al., 1992, 1995a; Kazen-Gillespie et al., 2000; Morgan et al., 2000; Qin et al., 2003; Yu et al., 2003). These genes, which encode for beta1, beta2, beta3 and beta4 subunits respectively, are expressed in human tissues including the brain, skeletal muscle and the heart (Candenas et al., 2006; Stevens et al., 2001). Of these, the beta1 and beta3 subunits have been demonstrated in the transverse tubules, and beta2 and beta4 subunits in the intercalated disks of murine ventricular myocytes (Maier et al., 2004).
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 36 40 36 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 103 104 100 101 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 178 185 175 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xenopus</italic>
###xml 286 290 283 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 403 404 397 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 414 495 408 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib8 bib33 bib35 bib39" ref-type="bibr">Chen et&#160;al., 2002; Meadows et&#160;al., 2002; Morgan et&#160;al., 2000; Patton et&#160;al., 1994</xref>
###xml 583 584 577 578 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 603 659 597 653 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib20 bib35 bib41" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995b; Morgan et&#160;al., 2000; Qu et&#160;al., 2001</xref>
###xml 708 709 702 703 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 729 799 723 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib12 bib28 bib52" ref-type="bibr">Fahmi et&#160;al., 2001; Lopez-Santiago et&#160;al., 2007; Watanabe et&#160;al., 2008</xref>
###xml 811 815 805 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 957 975 948 966 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib19" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995a</xref>
###xml 1062 1083 1053 1074 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib31" ref-type="bibr">Malhotra et&#160;al., 2000</xref>
###xml 1099 1103 1090 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1173 1174 1161 1162 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1292 1293 1280 1281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1318 1323 1306 1307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 1356 1360 1340 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1360 1361 1341 1342 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1410 1428 1391 1409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib20" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995b</xref>
###xml 178 185 <span type="species:ncbi:8355">Xenopus</span>
###xml 195 210 <span type="species:ncbi:10029">Chinese hamster</span>
###xml 233 238 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
It is possible that the presence of beta-subunits can affect both the function and expression of the Na+ channel. Firstly, studies in heterologous expression systems provided by Xenopus oocytes, Chinese hamster ovary (CHO) cells and human embryonic kidney (HEK) cells demonstrated that beta-subunits modify gating kinetics, including activation, inactivation and the recovery from inactivation of the Na+ channel (Chen et al., 2002; Meadows et al., 2002; Morgan et al., 2000; Patton et al., 1994). However, these alterations vary with the particular cell types used to express the Na+ channel subunits (Isom et al., 1995b; Morgan et al., 2000; Qu et al., 2001). Secondly, these subunits can also alter the Na+ current amplitude (Fahmi et al., 2001; Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007; Watanabe et al., 2008). Thirdly, beta-subunits contain domains that are structurally homologous to the V-set of the Ig superfamily, which includes cell adhesion molecules (CAMs) (Isom et al., 1995a). This permits cell-cell interaction and adhesion in cells expressing these subunits (Malhotra et al., 2000). Finally, the beta-subunits have been shown to regulate the expression density of the Na+ channel in the plasma membrane. Experiments using CHO and 1610 cell lines have demonstrated a 2- to 4-fold greater Na+ channel expression when alpha-subunits were co-expressed with beta1 subunits, than when these were expressed alone (Isom et al., 1995b).
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 27 31 27 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 221 226 218 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 315 342 312 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib28" ref-type="bibr">Lopez-Santiago et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 427 432 424 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN4B</italic>
###xml 444 473 441 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib34" ref-type="bibr">Medeiros-Domingo et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 479 484 476 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN1B</italic>
###xml 500 504 497 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 504 505 498 499 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 510 514 504 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 514 516 505 507 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1B</sub>
###xml 536 557 527 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib52" ref-type="bibr">Watanabe et&#160;al., 2008</xref>
###xml 668 673 659 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 673 676 664 667 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 731 736 722 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 736 739 727 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 850 855 841 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 855 858 846 849 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1011 1016 1002 1007 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1018 1023 1009 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1028 1033 1019 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1081 1086 1072 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1086 1089 1077 1080 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1213 1214 1204 1205 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1278 1283 1269 1274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1283 1286 1274 1277 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1295 1339 1286 1330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib38 bib45" ref-type="bibr">Papadatos et&#160;al., 2002; Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007a</xref>
###xml 203 207 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 740 744 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 859 863 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 935 939 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 970 974 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The presence or absence of beta-subunits has recently been associated with electrophysiological abnormalities in cardiac tissue. Surface electrocardiogram experiments carried out on genetically modified mice, lacking the Scn1b gene, have demonstrated a LQT-like phenotype, characterised by a prolonged QT interval (Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007). However, only two clinical reports thus far have associated mutations in the gene SCN4B with LQTS (Medeiros-Domingo et al., 2007) and SCN1B, encoding both beta1 and beta1B subunits with BrS (Watanabe et al., 2008). In the present study, we assessed, for the first time, electrophysiological properties in the ventricles of Scn3b-/- hearts compared to those shown in WT hearts. Firstly, Scn3b-/- mice were created using homologous recombination in embryonic stem (ES) cells. The phenotype of the resulting Scn3b-/- mice, including body weight and temperature, appeared similar to that of WT mice. Secondly, ventricles of such mice showed altered expression levels of Scn3b, Scn1b and Scn5a mRNA. Thirdly, studies in Langendorff-perfused Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated arrhythmogenic features. Finally, these corresponded to changes in the biophysical properties of the Na+ channel, with features similar to those previously reported in Scn5a+/- hearts (Papadatos et al., 2002; Stokoe et al., 2007a).
###end p 10
###begin title 11
Methods
###end title 11
###begin title 12
###xml 36 40 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Generation of Scn3b-deficient (-/-) mice
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 152 157 152 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 361 366 361 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 72 77 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
PCR amplification was used to generate homologous arms from the 129SvEv mouse genome, using primers designed to amplify a 5' arm spanning 2.0 kb of the Scn3b locus terminating downstream of the third coding exon splice acceptor (5'armF; tttgcggccgCAGCCTTGTATGAACCCAGGGTCTTTC and 5'armR; tttactagtCACCTCCTGGTGGCCATTTCGATACTC) and a 3' arm spanning 4.1 kb of the Scn3b locus commencing just upstream of the third coding exon splice donor (3'armF; tttggcgcgccGGTAAGCCTGAGGCCTGTAGTCTCTTC and 3'armR; tttggccggccGTGGACTTTAGTCCCATGTCCTCATTG).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 206 210 206 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LacZ</italic>
###xml 239 243 239 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">loxP</italic>
###xml 374 378 374 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LacZ</italic>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Afl</italic>
###xml 703 706 703 706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bcl</italic>
The arms were cloned into the plasmid pTK5IBLMNL (Paradigm Therapeutics Ltd, Cambridge, U.K.) using the restriction sites incorporated in the arm primers, such that the 5' and 3' arms flank an IRES-fronted LacZ reporter gene followed by a loxP-flanked PGKNeopA selectable marker. After homologous recombination, 191 bp of the 226 bp third coding exon is replaced by the IRESLacZ/PGKneo cassette. Putative targeted embryonic stem (ES) cells were identified by PCR using an external 5' screening primer (5'scr: CTGACATCTTCTCAGCAGATAACTGAC) in combination with a vector specific primer (DR2; ATCATGGCCCTACCATGCGCTAAACAC). Successfully targeted ES cells were further confirmed by Southern blot of AflII and BclI digested genomic DNA, using an external probe amplified from a genomic region downstream of the end of the 3' arm (using the primers 3'prF; AGATGTCCAGCGATACTGTTGAGGCAG and 3'prR; TGTGAGTCTTATTGGAGGTACAGTGTG), indicating that the integration had occurred legitimately.
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 53 58 53 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 141 161 141 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib3" ref-type="bibr">Bradley et&#160;al., 1984</xref>
###xml 543 548 543 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 979 984 979 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 984 987 984 987 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 988 992 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1044 1048 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 1178 1182 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Correctly targeted 129 SvEv ES cells, containing the Scn3b knockout (KO) allele were injected into host blastocysts as previously described (Bradley et al., 1984), generating male chimeras which were subsequently mated with 129 SvEv females. Pups from these crosses were screened with the original target screening PCR (using 5'scr and vector specific primer, DR2), to identify heterozygote animals and in further generations by a multiplex PCR designed to amplify a 204 bp region specific to the WT allele and a 334 bp region specific to the Scn3b KO allele. This allowed differentiation of each of the three possible genotypes (using primers hetF, GTCGTCTGCAGTGGAATGGGAGCAAAG; hetR, TGAAGAGACTACAGGCCTCAGGCTTAC; and Asc306, AATGGCCGCTTTTCTGGATTCATCGAC). All genotypes were observed at the expected Mendelian ratios. Routinely homozygous matings were established to produce the experimental cohorts and 129SvEv stock used as the WT controls. Male and female offspring of WT and Scn3b-/- mice were randomly selected for use in all experiments. Mice obtained were kept in cages at a room temperature of 21 +/- 1 degreesC in an animal facility with 12-hour light/dark cycles. The mice had free access to sterile rodent chow and water.
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 124 129 124 129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 129 132 129 132 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 959 971 959 971 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib27" ref-type="bibr">Lister, 1987</xref>
###xml 133 137 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 178 182 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 300 305 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 953 957 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
A series of tests were used to assess baseline metabolic and behavioural parameters and were performed on cohorts of WT and Scn3b-/- mice. Each cohort typically consisted of 5-8 mice of either sex at the age of 3-4 months. The metabolic tests included measuring the body weight and temperature. Each mouse was weighed monthly for up to 3 months and body temperature was measured using a rectal probe (World Precision Instruments, Florida, USA). The behavioural tests measured visual tracking, locomotor activity, touch sensitivity and anxiety. Firstly, visual tracking was assessed using an optokinetic drum apparatus (Paradigm Therapeutics, Cambridge, U.K.). Secondly, locomotor activity was measured as the distance travelled, in one hour, using the LABORAS system (Metris, Hoofddorp, The Netherlands). Finally, the percentage time spent in the open and closed arms of an elevated plus-maze apparatus was used to assess aversion to open spaces in the mice (Lister, 1987). All procedures conformed to the UK Animals (Scientific Procedures) Act 1986.
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 110 117 110 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ex vivo</italic>
###xml 34 38 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Randomly selected male and female mice (age 5-8 months) were killed by cervical dislocation in all RT-PCR and ex vivo experiments (Schedule 1: UK Animals (Scientific Procedures) Act 1986).
###end p 17
###begin title 18
Analysis of sodium channel alpha- and beta-subunit transcripts
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 60 65 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 71 75 67 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 116 121 109 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 121 124 114 117 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 350 355 343 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 355 358 348 351 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 365 366 358 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 444 447 437 438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#174;</sup>
###xml 673 686 664 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b, Scn5a,</italic>
###xml 691 696 682 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 125 129 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 359 363 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To quantify changes in the mRNA expression levels of sodium alpha- and beta-subunits in hearts obtained from WT and Scn3b-/- mice, RT-PCR experiments were performed on an ABI 7500 Fast cycler (Applied Biosystems, Warrington, U.K.). Total RNA was isolated from left atria (LA), right atria (RA), left ventricle (LV) and right ventricle (RV) of WT and Scn3b-/- mice (n = 3 each) using a Qiagen RNAeasy kit. Excised tissues were stored in RNAlater(R) (Ambion, Warrington, U.K.) to maintain the integrity of the RNA before isolation. The total RNA was reverse transcribed into cDNA using random hexamer primers and a SuperScript III kit (Invitrogen, Paisley, U.K.). Oligos for Scn3b, Scn5a, and Scn1b were FAM/TAMRA labelled (Applied Biosystems). All experiments were performed in triplicate.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 86 87 86 87 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</sub>
###xml 295 302 295 298 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;CT</sup>
The number of the copies of mRNA was calculated from its respective threshold cycle (CT) using a standard curve. Each value was normalized for the expression value of the housekeeper gene, glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate dehydrogenase (GAPDH) and expressed as a percentage of GAPDH expression (i.e. 2DeltaCT x 100).
###end p 20
###begin title 21
Preparation of Langendorff-perfused hearts for electrophysiological recordings
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 81 109 81 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 323 324 323 324 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 326 327 326 327 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 337 338 337 338 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 348 349 348 349 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 417 418 417 418 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 424 425 424 425 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1268 1270 1260 1262 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 42 48 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 1013 1025 <span type="species:ncbi:87540">water jacket</span>
The experiments used Langendorff-perfused murine hearts as previously described (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003). Hearts were rapidly excised whilst minimizing contact with the atria and ventricles, then submerged in ice-cold bicarbonate-buffered Krebs-Henseleit solution containing (mM): 119 NaCl, 25 NaHCO3, 4.0 KCl, 1.2 KH2PO4, 1.0 MgCl2, 1.8 CaCl2, 10 glucose and 2.0 sodium-pyruvate (pH 7.4) and bubbled with 95% O2/5% CO2 gas mixture (British Oxygen Company, Manchester, U.K.). Under the ice-cold buffer, excess tissues surrounding the heart were removed, leaving a 2-3 mm section of the aorta. This was cannulated and sealed, using a micro-aneurysm clip (Harvard Apparatus, Edenbridge, U.K.) to a 21-gauge tailor-made cannula. The latter was pre-filled with ice-cold buffer solution using a 1 ml syringe. The preparation was transferred and attached to a Langendorff system, and then retrogradely perfused, using the bicarbonate-buffered Krebs-Henseleit solution described above, warmed to 37 degreesC via a water jacket and circulator (Techne model C-85 A, Cambridge, U.K.). The warmed perfusate was initially passed through a 200 mum and 5 mum filter membrane (Millipore, Watford, U.K.), before being introduced into the aorta at a constant flow of 2-2.5 ml min-1 using a peristaltic pump (Watson-Marlow Bredel model 505S, Falmouth, Cornwall, U.K.). The cannulated hearts were perfused for 5 min before further testing. Viable, healthy hearts then regained a homogenous pink colouration and spontaneous rhythmic contraction. Hearts that did not demonstrate these features upon perfusion were instantly discarded.
###end p 22
###begin title 23
Bipolar electrogram recording
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 70 76 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 848 854 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
In all experiments analysing the ventricles of the isolated, perfused murine heart, paired platinum stimulating electrodes (1 mm interpole spacing) were positioned over the epicardial surface of the right ventricle. Ventricular activity was examined by recording from the epicardial surface of the left ventricle using a silver chloride (2 mm tip diameter) recording electrode (Linton Instruments, Harvard Apparatus, U.K.), which was manually positioned. The electrical signals recorded from these hearts resulted in bipolar electrogram (BEG) recordings. The paired platinum stimulating electrodes paced the epicardial surface of the right ventricle and the stimulation used a 2 ms square-wave stimuli at three times excitation threshold (Grass-Telefactor, U.K., Slough, U.K.). These signals were amplified and high-pass filtered for recordings of murine heart (30-1 kHz) using a Gould 2400S amplifier (Gould-Nicolet Technologies, Ilford, Essex, U.K.) and then digitised using an analogue to digital converter (CED 1401plus MKII, Cambridge Electronic Design, Cambridge, U.K.) at a sampling frequency of 5 kHz. All digitised data was then captured and analysed using Spike 2 software (Cambridge Electronic Design).
###end p 24
###begin title 25
Monophasic action potential recording and regular pacing
###end title 25
###begin p 26
###xml 156 213 156 213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib13 bib23 bib25" ref-type="bibr">Franz, 1999; Killeen et&#160;al., 2007; Knollmann et&#160;al., 2001</xref>
###xml 1178 1199 1178 1199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib6" ref-type="bibr">Casimiro et&#160;al., 2001</xref>
In addition to ventricular BEGs, monophasic action potentials (MAPs) of the ventricles were also recorded using an established contact-electrode technique (Franz, 1999; Killeen et al., 2007; Knollmann et al., 2001). The stimulating electrodes were positioned on the basal surface of the right ventricular epicardium and used to deliver electrical stimulation, as described above. Each isolated perfused heart underwent a period of regular pacing using 2 ms square-wave stimuli, delivered at three times the excitation threshold, at a basic cycle length (BCL) of 125 ms, for up to 20 min to record both epicardial and endocardial MAPs. Epicardial MAPs were recorded from the basal surface of the left ventricular epicardium using the silver chloride recording electrode. Endocardial MAPs were also obtained, from the left ventricular endocardium using a custom-made endocardial MAP electrode, constructed from two Teflon-coated (0.25 mm diameter) silver wires (99.99%) (Advent Research Materials Ltd. Oxford, U.K.), that were twisted together and galvanically chlorided. This electrode was inserted through a small access window carefully created in the interventricular septum (Casimiro et al., 2001). The tip of the electrode was rotated and positioned against the left ventricular free wall, maintaining stable contact pressure. Signals obtained from the recording electrode were amplified and low-pass filtered between 0.1 Hz and 1.0 kHz using the Gould 2400S amplifier (Gould-Nicolet Technologies) and digitised using the CED 1401plus MKII analogue to digital converter (Cambridge Electronic Design) as described above. Both epicardial and endocardial MAP waveforms were analysed using Spike2 software (Cambridge Electronic Design).
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 291 311 291 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib45" ref-type="bibr">Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007a</xref>
###xml 399 401 399 401 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">30</sub>
###xml 412 414 412 414 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 425 427 425 427 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 441 443 441 443 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 509 511 505 507 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 547 549 543 545 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 580 582 576 578 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 590 631 586 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib23 bib49" ref-type="bibr">Killeen et&#160;al., 2007; Thomas et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
MAPs that were used for analysis, satisfied previously established waveform characteristics including a stable baseline, a rapid upstroke phase with consistent amplitude, a smooth contoured repolarization, a stable duration and 100% repolarization achieved by a full return to the baseline (Stokoe et al., 2007a). These MAP waveforms were used to obtain action potential durations (APDs) at 30% (APD30), 50% (APD50), 70% (APD70) and 90% (APD90) repolarization. Transmural gradients of repolarization (DeltaAPD90) were calculated as endocardial APD90 value minus the epicardial APD90 value (Killeen et al., 2007; Thomas et al., 2007).
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Programmed electrical stimulation
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 145 199 145 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2 bib43" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003; Saumarez and Grace, 2000</xref>
###xml 328 329 328 329 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 398 399 398 399 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 413 414 413 414 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 416 417 416 417 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 455 456 455 456 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 541 542 541 542 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 544 545 544 545 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 574 575 574 575 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 776 777 776 777 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 779 780 779 780 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
Programmed electrical stimulation (PES) was used to assess ventricular arrhythmogenesis in each heart preparation and recorded as BEGs and MAPs (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003; Saumarez and Grace, 2000). The PES protocol first paced the heart for 25 s at the BCL. This was followed by cycles each consisting of an eight stimuli (S1) drive train at a CL of 125 ms followed by a ninth extra-stimulus (S2). The first S1-S2 interval (between the eighth S1 and S2 stimuli) equalled the pacing interval. Successive cycles progressively reduced the S1-S2 interval by 1 ms until the S2 stimulus could no longer evoke a ventricular deflection, at which point, the whole heart preparation reached the ventricular effective refractory period (VERP). VERP was hence defined as the longest S1-S2 interval that could not elicit a ventricular deflection.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 169 212 169 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib16 bib43" ref-type="bibr">Head et&#160;al., 2005; Saumarez and Grace, 2000</xref>
###xml 268 269 268 269 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 418 419 418 419 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 421 422 421 422 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 682 683 682 683 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 685 686 685 686 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 725 726 725 726 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 728 729 728 729 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 740 760 740 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib45" ref-type="bibr">Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007a</xref>
###xml 847 848 847 848 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 874 875 874 875 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 877 878 877 878 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
From the ventricular BEGs obtained, conduction curves were constructed, using paced electrogram fractionation analysis (PEFA), a procedure applied in clinical practice (Head et al., 2005; Saumarez and Grace, 2000). These curves plotted the response latencies of each S2 extra-stimulus, defined as the time difference between the extra-stimulus and the peak and troughs of the resulting BEG, against the corresponding S1-S2 interval. The electrogram duration (EGD) is characterised as the time difference between the first and last BEG peak and trough. The EGD ratios from corresponding conduction curves were calculated by normalizing the EGD of the BEG obtained from the shortest S1-S2 interval with the EGD of the longest S1-S2 interval (Stokoe et al., 2007a). The initial conduction latency was defined as the time difference from the initial S2 stimulus applied at the S1-S2 interval of 125 ms and the initial deflection of the resulting electrogram response.
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Ventricular myocyte isolation
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 59 60 59 60 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 433 434 433 434 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 443 445 443 445 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 502 504 502 504 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 643 645 643 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 735 736 735 736 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 854 855 854 855 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 646 652 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
A solution consisting of (in mM): 120 NaCl, 5.4 KCl, 5 MgSO4, 5.5 sodium-pyruvate, 10 glucose, 20 taurine and 10 HEPES was used as the basic isolation buffer. This was used to make the following solutions. Firstly, an NTA buffer consisted of the isolation buffer and 5 mM nitrilotriacetic acid (NTA). The pH of this buffer was adjusted to 6.95. Secondly, a digestion buffer, which contained the isolation buffer to which 0.25 mM CaCl2, 1 mg ml-1 collagenase type 2 (Worthington, NJ, U.S.A.) and 1 mg ml-1 hyaluronidase (Sigma-Aldrich, Poole, U.K.) was added. Thirdly, a stop buffer was created, which contained the isolation buffer and 2 mg ml-1 bovine serum albumin (Sigma-Aldrich). Fourthly, the isolation buffer to which 0.6 mM CaCl2 was added, was created as the wash buffer. Finally, a storage buffer, similar to the wash buffer but with 1.2 mM CaCl2, was made. All the buffers created, except for the NTA buffer, had their pH adjusted to 7.4.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 265 267 265 267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 16 20 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 362 374 <span type="species:ncbi:87540">water jacket</span>
Hearts of adult mice were rapidly excised and submerged in ice-cold isolation buffer, prior to whole-heart isolation. The hearts were then perfused for 2 min with NTA buffer in a retrograde fashion using a variable speed peristaltic pump at a flow rate of 3.5 ml ms-1 (Autoclude EV045, Essex, U.K.). Before perfusion, the buffer was warmed to 37 degreesC with a water jacket and circulator (Techne model RB-5 A, Cambridge, U.K.). Following this, the heart was then perfused in the same fashion with the digestion buffer for 12-15 min. Using watchmaker's forceps, ventricular tissue was taken from the whole heart and placed in the stop buffer. After transferring into a 15 ml test tube, gentle trituration was used to isolate single myocytes from the harvested cardiac tissue. After 5 min for the cells to settle, the supernatant was then gently removed. The isolated cells were then washed using wash buffer. Following a further 5 min, the isolated myocytes were resuspended and stored in the storage buffer. After each step after harvesting the cells, isolated myocytes were checked under a light microscope to confirm cell integrity. Live myocytes appeared as smooth and rod-shaped cells.
###end p 33
###begin title 34
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
INa measurements
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 105 106 105 106 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 126 131 126 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 131 134 131 134 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 550 551 540 541 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 574 575 564 565 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 894 895 884 885 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 906 907 896 897 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 978 979 968 969 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1015 1016 1005 1006 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1108 1109 1098 1099 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1120 1121 1110 1111 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
The biophysical experiments studied the activation, inactivation and recovery from inactivation in the Na+ channels of WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. These experiments were carried out at a physiological temperature of 37 degreesC, using the whole-cell configuration, with an Axopatch 700B amplifier (Molecular Devices, Berkshire, U.K.). Borosilicate glass pipettes (0.86 mm outer diameter; Harvard Apparatus, Kent, U.K) with a resistance of 1.5-2.5 MOmega were used. These pipettes were filled with (in mM): 70.26 CsCl, 24.74 Cs-aspartate, 10 HEPES, 1 Na2ATP, 4 MgATP, 1.37 MgCl2, and 10 Cs-BAPTA, adjusted to pH 7.2 using CsOH. Cells were loaded into a chamber which was mounted on the stage of a Nikon TE2000 Eclipse microscope (Nikon, Kingston, U.K.). These cells were initially perfused with an extracellular bath solution, which contained (in mM): 145 NaCl, 5 KCl, 10 glucose, 10 HEPES, 1 MgCl2 and 1 CaCl2, adjusted to pH 7.4 using NaOH. To achieve optimum voltage control, Na+ currents were recorded in a low [Na+] solution. This solution contained (in mM): 10 NaCl, 140 CsCl, 10 glucose, 10 HEPES, 1 MgCl2 and 1 CaCl2, adjusted to pH 7.4 using CsOH. The currents obtained were filtered at a 10 kHz high frequency cut off and digitised at 100 kHz using pClamp 10 software (Molecular Devices). In each experiment, the series resistance was compensated by at least 70% and each protocol used a holding potential of -100 mV.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 278 279 278 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 279 280 279 280 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sub>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 403 404 403 404 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sub>
###xml 548 549 548 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V</italic>
###xml 549 550 549 550 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sub>
###xml 574 575 574 575 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 589 590 589 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 590 592 590 592 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
###xml 640 641 640 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 641 643 641 643 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
###xml 681 682 681 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 682 684 682 684 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
###xml 696 697 696 697 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 723 724 723 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 724 726 724 726 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
###xml 798 799 798 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 831 832 831 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</italic>
###xml 871 872 871 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">z</italic>
###xml 915 916 915 916 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 943 944 943 944 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 945 958 945 958 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">extracellular</sub>
###xml 974 975 974 975 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 976 989 976 989 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">intracellular</sub>
###xml 1002 1003 1002 1003 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1003 1005 1003 1005 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
###xml 1089 1090 1089 1090 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1090 1092 1090 1092 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</sub>
Firstly, the voltage dependence of activation was studied by applying depolarizing pulses of 20 ms duration. These pulses were applied over series of voltage steps from -100 mV, in 10 mV increments, to 70 mV. The resulting currents were normalized against the cell capacitance (Cm) and plotted against time. The peak current densities (pA/pF) were calculated by dividing the peak currents amplitude by Cm. The current-voltage relationship was obtained by plotting the values of the peak current density against each corresponding membrane voltage (Vm). The values of peak Na+ conductance (gNa) values were determined from the equationwhere INa was the peak current density and the ENa was the [Na+] reversal potential. The ENa was assumed to be 42.6 mV. This was based on the Nernst equation;where R is the universal gas constant, T is the absolute temperature at 310 K, z is the valence of the ionic species at 1, F is Faraday's constant, [Na+]extracellular = 10 mM and [Na+]intracellular = 2 mM. The gNa values calculated from each myocyte were normalized against the corresponding peak gNa value. When plotted against the test-pulse voltage, the data assumed a sigmoid function, increasing with membrane potential.
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 635 636 635 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V</italic>
###xml 636 639 636 639 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1/2</sub>
###xml 659 660 659 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 674 675 674 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">y</italic>
Secondly, the voltage dependence of inactivation was examined using pre-pulses of 500 ms duration. These pre-pulses were applied over a voltage range from -120 mV to -20 mV in 10 mV increments. Each pre-pulse was followed by a test pulse to -20 mV at a duration of 10 ms. The peak currents obtained were normalized against the peak current recorded at the pre-pulse of -120 mV. The normalized currents were then plotted against the pre-pulse voltage. The data assumed a sigmoid function, decreasing with membrane potential. Both inactivation and activation data were fitted with a Boltzmann function:yielding the half-maximal voltage (V1/2) and slope factor (k) values. The y values corresponded to the normalized current values.
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 207 208 207 208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 630 631 630 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 631 632 631 632 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</sub>
###xml 637 638 637 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 638 639 638 639 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 708 711 708 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 711 712 709 710 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</sub>
###xml 717 720 715 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 720 721 716 717 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 796 797 792 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">y</italic>
Finally, to determine the time course of recovery from inactivation, a protocol consisting of 18 cycles was employed. Each cycle consisted of a 1 s pre-pulse to -20 mV, used to achieve inactivation of the Na+ channels, followed by a return to the voltage of -100 mV to allow recovery of the channels. With each cycle, the duration of recovery increased from 1 to 250 ms. A 50 ms test pulse to -20 mV determined the current from the recovered channels. The currents recorded were normalized against the current obtained from each pre-pulse applied. A bi-exponential function was fitted to the recovery from inactivation data,where Af and As are the amplitude of the fast and slow inactivating components, and tauf and taus are the time constants of the fast and slow components, respectively. The y values correspond to the normalized current values. Data was analysed using Signal 2.16 (Cambridge Electronic Design) and all curve fits were performed using OriginPro 8 (OriginLab Corporation, MA, USA).
###end p 38
###begin title 39
Data analysis and statistical procedures
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 169 174 169 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 174 177 174 177 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
For experiments in mRNA expression levels, the single-factor analysis of variance for independent samples (ANOVA) test was used to compare the difference between WT and Scn3b-/- tissue samples (Microsoft EXCEL Analysis ToolPak) to show significant changes in expression of the mRNA.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 117 122 117 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 122 125 122 125 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 193 194 193 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
Whole-heart BEG and MAP data were initially imported into Microsoft EXCEL. The ANOVA test was used to compare WT and Scn3b-/- data sets (Microsoft EXCEL Analysis ToolPak). Calculated values of P < 0.05 were considered significant. Results are shown as means +/- S.E.M values.
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 3 4 3 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 94 95 94 95 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 165 170 165 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 170 173 170 173 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 255 256 255 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
An F-test was used firstly to confirm the normal distribution of the data acquired from the Na+ current recordings (Microsoft EXCEL Analysis ToolPak) made in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. Depending on the type of variance, the appropriate form of the Student t test was applied to analyze the differences between two groups of data.
###end p 42
###begin title 43
Results
###end title 43
###begin title 44
###xml 51 55 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Gene targeting of Scn3b and generation of knockout mice
###end title 44
###begin p 45
###xml 15 19 15 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 19 20 16 17 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 75 79 72 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 79 80 73 74 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 114 118 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LacZ</italic>
###xml 136 142 130 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;1</xref>
###xml 142 143 136 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 235 240 229 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 353 358 347 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 649 652 643 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Afl</italic>
###xml 759 762 753 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bcl</italic>
###xml 844 850 838 844 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;1</xref>
###xml 850 851 844 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 873 878 867 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 878 881 872 875 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 930 936 924 930 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;1</xref>
###xml 936 937 930 931 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 1178 1183 1172 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1183 1186 1177 1180 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 534 539 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To disrupt the beta3 coding region, 191 bp of the 226 bp third exon of the beta3 sequence was replaced by the IRESLacZ/pGKneo cassette (Fig. 1A). The 5' arm of the plasmid used to generate the mutant contained a 2.0 kb fragment of the Scn3b locus terminating downstream of the third coding exon splice acceptor, and a 3' arm which spanned 4.1 kb of the Scn3b locus commencing just upstream of the third coding exon splice donor. Successfully targeted ES cells were screened by Southern blot using an external 3' probe (amplified from mouse genomic DNA using 3'prF; AGATGTCCAGCGATACTGTTGAGGCAG and 3'prR; TGTGAGTCTTATTGGAGGTACAGTGTG). Digestion with AflII yielded a 7.7 kb endogenous band and a 12.6 kb bp targeted band as predicted. Similar experiments using BclI resulted in a 7.2 kb endogenous band and the predicted 7.8 kb bp targeted band (Fig. 1B). Homozygous mutant (Scn3b-/-) offspring were identified using PCR screening (Fig. 1C). The primers used (hetF, GTCGTCTGCAGTGGAATGGGAGCAAAG; hetR, TGAAGAGACTACAGGCCTCAGGCTTAC; and Asc306, AATGGCCGCTTTTCTGGATTCATCGAC) resulted in the generation of a 204 bp band from the wild-type (WT) (+/+) allele, and a 334 bp band from the Scn3b-/- (-/-) allele. Both bands were present in the heterozygote (+/-) allele. A water control was used to confirm the specificity of the PCR primers.
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 31 36 31 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 36 39 36 39 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 185 192 185 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl1" ref-type="table">Table&#160;1</xref>
###xml 292 297 292 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 297 300 297 300 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 307 314 307 314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl1" ref-type="table">Table 1</xref>
###xml 40 44 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 135 139 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 179 183 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 301 305 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To assess the phenotype of the Scn3b-/- mice, both metabolic and behavioural tests were used. The body weight and temperature of these mice were similar to those obtained from WT mice (Table 1). Additionally, vision, locomotor activity and anxiety tests showed similar results in both WT and Scn3b-/- mice (Table 1).
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 28 29 28 29 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 50 56 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
mRNA expression levels of Na+ channel subunits in murine ventricles
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 46 51 46 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 92 97 92 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 144 149 144 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 149 152 149 152 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 180 185 180 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 236 241 236 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 241 244 241 244 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 430 431 430 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 441 445 441 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 455 460 452 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 462 467 459 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 487 488 484 485 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 497 502 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 512 517 505 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 615 616 608 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 626 631 619 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 631 634 624 627 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 660 661 653 654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 754 755 747 748 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</sub>
###xml 576 581 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The mRNA expression studies demonstrated that Scn3b mRNA was not present and an increase in Scn1b mRNA in both the left and right ventricles of Scn3b-/- hearts. An increase in the Scn5a mRNA was observed only in the right ventricles of Scn3b-/- hearts. In all cases, the mRNA expression in the left ventricles was consistently higher. Reverse-transcriptase PCR (RT-PCR) was used to investigate mRNA expression levels of sodium (Na+) channel beta-subunits Scn3b, Scn1b, and the cardiac Na+ channel alpha-subunit, Scn5a, in tissue obtained from the right and left ventricles of mouse wild-type (WT) (RV+/+ and LV+/+; n = 3) and Scn3b-/- hearts (RV-/- and LV-/-; n = 3). The number of the copies of mRNA was calculated from its respective threshold cycle (CT) using a standard curve. Each value was normalized to the corresponding expression of the housekeeping gene, glyceraldehyde-3-phosphate dehydrogenase (GAPDH).
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 285 292 285 288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;CT</sup>
###xml 332 336 328 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 336 337 329 330 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 348 353 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 453 459 446 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;2</xref>
###xml 459 460 452 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 476 477 469 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 483 484 476 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 530 535 523 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 535 538 528 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 547 548 540 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 610 615 603 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 143 148 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
This made comparison between samples possible by correcting for any variation between the quantity of mRNA isolated from the WT and transgenic mouse hearts. Transcript expression was expressed as relative abundances of mRNA expression, calculated as a % of the GAPDH expression (i.e. 2DeltaCT x 100). Firstly, the mRNA encoding the beta3 subunits, Scn3b, was expressed at statistically similar levels in both the left and right ventricles of WT hearts (Fig. 2A, black column, n = 3, P < 0.05). In contrast, both the ventricles of Scn3b-/- hearts (n = 3), as expected, did not show any detectable expression of Scn3b mRNA.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 52 57 52 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 57 60 57 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 69 75 69 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;2</xref>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B,</italic>
###xml 139 144 139 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 198 199 198 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 218 224 218 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;2</xref>
###xml 224 225 224 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 302 303 298 299 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 313 318 309 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 365 370 361 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 370 373 366 369 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 428 433 424 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 433 436 429 432 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 475 480 471 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 498 499 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 546 551 542 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 551 554 547 550 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 629 634 625 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
