###xml 671 672 667 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 714 719 710 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 724 729 720 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 800 805 796 801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 805 808 801 804 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 817 818 813 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 829 830 825 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
Secondly, both the left and right ventricles of the Scn3b-/- hearts (Fig. 2B, white column) showed an increase in the expression levels of Scn1b mRNA, relative to corresponding values in WT hearts (P < 0.05). Finally, Fig. 2C confirms the expression of the mRNA encoding for the alpha-subunit of the Na+ channel, Scn5a, in both ventricles of WT (black columns) and Scn3b-/- (white columns) hearts. The left ventricles of WT and Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated similar levels of Scn5a mRNA expression (P > 0.05). However, the right ventricles of the Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated a small but significant increase in the expression of Scn5a mRNA, than that shown in WT hearts (P < 0.05). Thus, mRNA expression levels of Scn1b and Scn5a were always higher in the left than in the right ventricles of WT and Scn3b-/- hearts (n = 3 each, P < 0.05).
###end p 50
###begin title 51
Analysis of BEG recordings during PES
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 91 96 91 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 96 99 96 99 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 251 256 251 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 256 259 256 259 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 365 370 365 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 370 373 370 373 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 456 461 456 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 461 464 461 464 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 505 510 505 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 510 513 510 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 892 946 892 946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2 bib43" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003; Saumarez and Grace, 2000</xref>
###xml 1099 1100 1099 1100 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1160 1161 1160 1161 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1177 1178 1177 1178 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1207 1208 1207 1208 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1210 1211 1210 1211 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1391 1392 1391 1392 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 260 266 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 842 848 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
The mRNA expression changes were correlated with a ventricular arrhythmogenic phenotype in Scn3b-/- hearts. This was demonstrated in electrophysiological experiments that assessed ventricular arrhythmogenicity in isolated, Langendorff-perfused WT and Scn3b-/- murine hearts. This was achieved by obtaining bipolar electrogram (BEG) (first series; 6 WT hearts and 7 Scn3b-/- hearts) and monophasic action potential (MAP) (second series; 14 WT hearts and 17 Scn3b-/- hearts, third series; 4 WT hearts and 4 Scn3b-/- hearts) recordings from the left ventricles. BEGs and MAPs were obtained once the preparations had regained a steady state after 10 min following mounting. BEG recordings were obtained during programmed electrical stimulation (PES). This procedure has been used in clinical situations to assess arrhythmogenicity and applied to murine hearts as described on previous occasions (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003; Saumarez and Grace, 2000). Hearts were initially paced at a basic cycle length (BCL) of 125 ms for 25 s. Subsequent cycles used a drive train each consisting of eight stimuli (S1) at the same BCL, followed by a premature extra-stimulus (S2). The initial S2 stimulus was imposed at an S1-S2 interval of 125 ms. With each cycle, this interval was reduced by 1 ms, until either the ventricular effective refractory period (VERP) was reached, at which point the premature S2 did not trigger a response or resulted in ventricular tachycardia (VT).
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 0 6 0 6 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;3</xref>
###xml 146 147 146 147 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 149 150 149 150 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 234 235 234 235 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 280 281 280 281 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 445 451 445 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;3</xref>
###xml 451 452 451 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 474 475 474 475 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 477 478 477 478 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 499 500 499 500 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 558 559 558 559 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 561 562 561 562 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 665 670 665 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 670 673 670 673 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 713 719 713 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;3</xref>
###xml 719 720 719 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
Fig. 3 shows examples of BEG traces obtained during PES. Each trace demonstrates results from the final cycles that corresponded to the shortest S1-S2 intervals. The single vertical marks below each recording indicate the successive S1 stimuli and the double vertical marks, the S2 extra-stimuli. Furthermore, each trace contains stimulus artefacts that occurred at regular CL, followed by their resulting electrogram. In the case of WT hearts (Fig. 3A), shortening of the S1-S2 interval led to an S2 extra-stimulus that did not elicit an electrogram. This S1-S2 interval corresponded to the VERP. In contrast, under such circumstances, a significant proportion of Scn3b-/- hearts showed ventricular arrhythmias (Fig. 3B).
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 246 270 246 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib43" ref-type="bibr">Saumarez and Grace, 2000</xref>
###xml 340 345 340 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kcne1</italic>
###xml 345 348 345 348 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 350 378 350 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 381 386 381 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 386 396 386 392 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
###xml 398 437 394 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib16 bib46" ref-type="bibr">Head et&#160;al., 2005; Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007b</xref>
###xml 443 448 439 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 448 451 444 447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 453 473 449 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib45" ref-type="bibr">Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007a</xref>
###xml 490 496 486 492 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 496 497 492 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 498 499 494 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 513 514 509 510 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 573 579 569 575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;3</xref>
###xml 801 807 797 803 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 807 808 803 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 810 811 806 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 817 822 813 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 822 825 818 821 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 827 833 823 829 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 833 834 829 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 836 837 832 833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 864 870 860 866 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 870 871 866 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 873 874 869 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 896 897 892 893 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 922 923 918 919 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 925 926 921 922 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1095 1101 1091 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 1101 1102 1097 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 1104 1105 1100 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 1127 1128 1123 1124 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1154 1155 1150 1151 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1157 1158 1153 1154 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1465 1466 1461 1462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1498 1499 1494 1495 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1501 1502 1497 1498 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 475 481 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
Conduction curves were then derived from the BEG recordings obtained during PES, using paced electrogram fractionation analysis (PEFA), a procedure that has been used to assess clinical risk of ventricular arrhythmogenicity on earlier occasions (Saumarez and Grace, 2000). It has also been previously applied to assess arrhythmogenicity in Kcne1-/- (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003), Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ (Head et al., 2005; Stokoe et al., 2007b) and Scn5a+/- (Stokoe et al., 2007a) murine hearts. Fig. 4A-D illustrates S2-induced BEG waveforms at a faster time base than shown in Fig. 3 in order to demonstrate differences in electrogram duration (EGD). This was defined as the time interval between the first and last deflection of each electrogram waveform. These waveforms were obtained during PES of WT (Fig. 4A, B) and Scn3b-/- (Fig. 4C, D) hearts. The waveforms in Fig. 4A, C were induced by the S2 stimuli at the longest S1-S2 intervals that were identical to the BCL, employed at the beginning of the procedure. The duration of these waveforms were defined as the initial EGD. The waveforms in Fig. 4B, D were induced by the S2 stimuli at the shortest S1-S2 intervals that could elicit an electrogram response, at the end of the procedure. The duration of these waveforms were defined as the final EGD. The EGD ratio was calculated as the final EGD divided by the initial EGD. The initial conduction latency was calculated as the time difference from the initial S2 extra-stimulus applied at the S1-S2 interval of 125 ms and the resulting BEG.
###end p 54

###xml 0 6 0 6 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>

###xml 483 488 483 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 488 491 488 491 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 523 524 523 524 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 526 527 526 527 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 539 540 539 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</italic>
###xml 598 599 598 599 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 617 623 617 623 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;4</xref>
###xml 623 624 623 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 686 691 686 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>

###xml 1268 1271 1264 1267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1387 1388 1379 1380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1394 1401 1386 1393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl3" ref-type="table">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1470 1471 1458 1459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1477 1478 1465 1466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1487 1494 1475 1482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl2" ref-type="table">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1510 1515 1498 1503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1515 1518 1503 1506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1609 1610 1595 1596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1634 1635 1618 1619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1641 1642 1625 1626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1659 1664 1643 1648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1664 1667 1648 1651 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1751 1752 1731 1732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1761 1775 1741 1755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl2 tbl3" ref-type="table">Tables 2&#160;and&#160;3</xref>
Fig. 4E shows examples of the conduction curves in WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. Each of the curves plots the latencies of each peak and trough of each deflection contained in the electrogram from the S2 stimulus against the corresponding S1-S2 interval. Such curves demonstrate increases in the degree of spread of each electrogram and conduction latency as S1-S2 interval shortens. However, these changes are more marked in Scn3b-/- hearts. A greater increase in the EGD was observed in Scn3b-/- hearts with shortening of the S1-S2 interval, (D, filled circles) compared to the EGD shown in WT hearts (B, clear circles). Fig. 4E also demonstrates the significantly shorter VERP observed in Scn3b-/- hearts than in WT hearts. Tables 2 and 3 summarise the VERP, initial and final EGD values, EGD ratios and conduction latencies obtained from the PEFA analysis of WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. It was possible to determine a VERP in only 2 out 7 Scn3b-/- hearts, with the remaining 5 hearts demonstrating PES-induced VT (Table 3). Nevertheless, the mean S1-S2 interval at which VERP and arrhythmogenicity occurred in Scn3b-/- hearts was 24.7 +/- 1.6 ms (n = 7 hearts), which was significantly shorter than the VERP of the WT hearts studied (31.2 +/- 1.5 ms, n = 6, P < 0.05). Scn3b-/- hearts showed significantly larger initial and final EGD values (17.1 +/- 3.8 ms and 34.6 +/- 6.6 ms respectively, n = 7; Table 3) compared to those of WT hearts (2.3 +/- 0.4 ms and 2.8 +/- 0.4 ms, n = 6, P < 0.05; Table 2). Furthermore, Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated a larger mean EGD ratio than that shown in WT hearts (2.1 +/- 0.2 ms, n = 7 vs. 1.3 +/- 0.1 ms n = 6, P < 0.05). WT and Scn3b-/- hearts both showed similar conduction latencies (8.0 +/- 0.4 ms vs. 8.3 +/- 0.2 ms P > 0.05; Tables 2 and 3).
###end p 55
###begin title 56
Analysis of MAP recordings during PES
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 259 264 259 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 264 267 264 267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 445 451 445 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 497 498 497 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 504 509 504 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 509 512 509 512 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 514 515 514 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 517 518 517 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 605 606 605 606 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 608 609 608 609 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 697 698 697 698 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 741 742 741 742 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 909 910 909 910 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 962 967 962 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 967 970 967 970 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1073 1133 1073 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib11 bib15 bib23" ref-type="bibr">Fabritz et&#160;al., 2003; Guo et&#160;al., 1999; Killeen et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 1261 1266 1261 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1266 1276 1266 1272 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
###xml 1292 1333 1288 1329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib23 bib48" ref-type="bibr">Killeen et&#160;al., 2007; Thomas et&#160;al., 2008</xref>
###xml 1277 1283 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
Analysis of MAP recordings permitted a closer differentiation of hearts with arrhythmogenic and non-arrhythmogenic phenotypes as well as of monomorphic and polymorphic VT. MAP waveforms were compared during PES in a second series of isolated, perfused WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. Each heart was subjected to an application of a single procedure of PES. This made it possible to determine when VT occurred, whether it was monomorphic or polymorphic. Fig. 5 illustrates MAP recordings obtained from WT (A) and Scn3b-/- (B, C) hearts during the final cycles of a PES procedure that corresponded to the shortest S1-S2 intervals. In each panel, the single vertical mark below each recording indicates the S1 stimuli and the double vertical mark the S2 extra-stimulus. The traces also show the corresponding stimulus artefacts that occurred at a regular CL, closely followed by their elicited MAP. MAPs in response to S1 stimuli were consistent in waveform in both WT and Scn3b-/- hearts, with each AP demonstrating a stable baseline, rapid upstroke and smooth repolarisation phase (Fabritz et al., 2003; Guo et al., 1999; Killeen et al., 2007). Neither demonstrated spontaneous events such as early or delayed afterdepolarizations that were reported in hypokalaemic and Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ murine hearts (Killeen et al., 2007; Thomas et al., 2008).
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 0 6 0 6 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 6 7 6 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 118 119 118 119 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 249 250 249 250 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 330 335 330 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 335 338 335 338 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 385 391 385 391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 391 392 391 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 413 419 413 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 419 420 419 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 436 437 436 437 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 678 685 678 685 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl4" ref-type="table">Table 4</xref>
###xml 751 752 751 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 768 771 768 771 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 780 781 780 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 893 894 893 894 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 896 897 896 897 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 999 1000 997 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1098 1103 1096 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1103 1106 1101 1104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1188 1189 1184 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1290 1291 1286 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1298 1299 1294 1295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1323 1328 1319 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1328 1331 1324 1327 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1382 1383 1378 1379 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1385 1386 1381 1382 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1417 1418 1411 1412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1482 1483 1476 1477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1513 1518 1507 1512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1518 1521 1512 1515 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1530 1531 1524 1525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1537 1538 1531 1532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1598 1604 1590 1596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 1604 1608 1596 1600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B, C</italic>
###xml 1687 1693 1679 1685 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 1693 1694 1685 1686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 1767 1774 1757 1764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl5" ref-type="table">Table 5</xref>
###xml 2034 2040 2022 2028 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;5</xref>
###xml 2040 2041 2028 2029 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
Fig. 5A shows a typical MAP recording obtained during the final cycles of the PES procedure in a WT heart. The first S2 extra-stimulus that is displayed, gave rise to an action potential. However, the heart was refractory in response to the second S2 extra-stimulus, thereby permitting the determination of the VERP. In contrast, Scn3b-/- hearts showed episodes of either monomorphic (Fig. 5B) or polymorphic VT (Fig. 5C) following an S2 extra-stimulus. Monomorphic VT showed successive ventricular deflections that were of similar waveform and amplitude. Polymorphic VT demonstrated varying intervals between each successive deflection with irregular amplitudes and waveforms. Table 4 summarises the properties of the MAP waveforms during PES in WT (n = 14) and Scn3b-/- hearts (n = 17). It lists the VERP shown in non-arrhythmogenic hearts. Where the heart was arrhythmogenic, it lists the S1-S2 interval value, which would be less than the VERP. The WT hearts had a mean VERP of 39.3 +/- 1.6 ms (n = 14). PES did not induce VT in any of the WT hearts. In contrast to WT hearts, only 7 out of 17 Scn3b-/- hearts were non-arrhythmogenic. These hearts had a mean VERP of 43.3 +/- 4.4 ms (n = 7). This was not significantly different from the corresponding mean VERP, recorded in WT hearts (n = 14, P > 0.05). The remaining Scn3b-/- hearts were arrhythmogenic in response to a mean S1-S2 interval of <29.3 +/- 2.4 ms (n = 10). This was significantly shorter than the VERP of the WT (n = 14) and non-arrhythmogenic Scn3b-/- hearts (n = 7; P < 0.05). The mean duration of the VT was 98.85 +/- 39.8 s (Fig. 5B, C). In 5 out of the 10 arrhythmogenic hearts, the hearts showed monomorphic VT (Fig. 5B). The mean duration of episodes of monomorphic VT was 100.6 +/- 46.4 s (Table 5). In 4 hearts out of 10 arrhythmogenic hearts, the hearts demonstrated polymorphic VT. The mean duration of the polymorphic VT was 27.3 +/- 13.8 s. Finally, PES-induced VT in the remaining heart began as a monomorphic VT and deteriorated into polymorphic VT (Fig. 5C). This persisted until spontaneous termination of the episode.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 57 60 57 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Endocardial and epicardial MAP recordings in WT and Scn3b-/- hearts
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 67 72 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 72 75 72 75 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 130 132 130 132 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 221 223 217 219 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 369 411 365 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib23 bib46" ref-type="bibr">Killeen et&#160;al., 2007; Stokoe et&#160;al., 2007b</xref>
###xml 896 898 892 894 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">30</sub>
###xml 909 911 905 907 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 922 924 918 920 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 938 940 934 936 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
Comparison of endocardial and epicardial recordings suggested that Scn3b-/- hearts showed a shorter endocardial and epicardial APD90 which nevertheless demonstrated a normal transmural gradient of repolarization, DeltaAPD90. Previous studies have demonstrated that arrhythmogenic properties were associated with abnormal differences in epicardial and endocardial APDs (Killeen et al., 2007; Stokoe et al., 2007b). The present investigation made similar experiments, which recorded MAPs at the BCL from the left ventricular epicardium and endocardium of a third series of hearts. Measurements were obtained from five separate 20 s periods during regular pacing. For each period taken, the recording electrode was repositioned to obtain independent readings from different regions of the ventricle. This was to ensure the values obtained were comparable. Action potential duration (APD) at 30% (APD30), 50% (APD50), 70% (APD70) and 90% (APD90) repolarization values were obtained from the MAPs.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 0 14 0 14 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl6 tbl7" ref-type="table">Tables 6 and 7</xref>
###xml 112 117 112 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 117 120 117 120 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 228 230 228 230 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">30</sub>
###xml 235 237 235 237 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 242 244 242 244 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 278 279 278 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 365 371 357 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;6</xref>
###xml 371 372 363 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 405 410 397 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 410 413 402 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 518 519 502 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 525 526 509 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 549 554 533 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 554 557 538 541 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 572 574 556 558 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 582 584 566 568 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 652 654 636 638 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 662 664 646 648 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 697 699 681 683 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sub>
###xml 707 709 691 693 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 796 802 776 782 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;6</xref>
###xml 802 803 782 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 844 849 824 829 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 849 852 829 832 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 915 916 891 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 922 923 898 899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 947 949 923 925 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">30</sub>
###xml 957 959 933 935 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">50</sub>
###xml 995 1000 971 976 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1000 1003 976 979 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1012 1013 988 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1074 1076 1046 1048 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1152 1154 1124 1126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1173 1175 1145 1147 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1177 1197 1149 1169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib23" ref-type="bibr">Killeen et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 1204 1209 1176 1181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1209 1212 1181 1184 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1259 1261 1227 1229 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1300 1301 1264 1265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1311 1317 1275 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;6</xref>
###xml 1317 1318 1281 1282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 1397 1402 1361 1366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1402 1405 1366 1369 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Tables 6 and 7 summarise the APD values obtained from the epicardium and endocardium. Endocardial APD values in Scn3b-/- hearts were significantly shorter than their corresponding WT endocardial values. Thus, the endocardial APD30, APD50, APD70 and APD90 recorded in WT hearts (n = 4) were 10.5 +/- 1.4, 18.8 +/- 2.1, 31.2 +/- 2.9 and 53.6 +/- 2.7 ms respectively (Fig. 6A). The same measurements made in Scn3b-/- hearts demonstrated APD values of 6.2 +/- 0.1 ms, 12.3 +/- 1.2 ms, 20.2 +/- 1.6 ms and 41.0 +/- 3.8 ms (n = 4, P < 0.05). Furthermore, Scn3b-/- epicardial APD70 and APD90 values were also significantly shorter than their respective WT APD70 and APD90 values. Thus, the epicardial APD70 and APD90 values obtained from WT hearts were 17.7 +/- 1.6 ms and 38.7 +/- 2.8 ms respectively (Fig. 6B). Equivalent measurements obtained from Scn3b-/- hearts were 10.2 +/- 0.8 ms and 27.5 +/- 2.3 ms respectively (n = 4, P < 0.05). Epicardial APD30 and APD50 values were both similar in WT and Scn3b-/- hearts (P > 0.05). The transmural gradient of repolarization (DeltaAPD90) was quantified as the difference between the values of the endocardial APD90 and epicardial APD90 (Killeen et al., 2007). The Scn3b-/- and WT hearts showed similar positive DeltaAPD90 (14.0 +/- 3.4 ms vs. 15.4 +/- 4.4 ms, P > 0.05) (Fig. 6C). This is despite a decrease in epicardial and endocardial values observed in Scn3b-/- hearts.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
###xml 2 3 2 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
Na+ current recordings in isolated ventricular myocytes
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 40 45 40 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 45 48 45 48 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 266 271 266 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 271 274 271 274 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 318 322 318 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 322 323 319 320 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 338 339 335 336 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 447 452 444 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 452 455 449 452 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
The electrophysiological changes in the Scn3b-/- whole heart was correlated with a reduction in the peak Na+ current and a shift in the inactivation curve in the negative direction. The activation properties and recovery from inactivation remained similar in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. The effects of the expression of beta3 subunits on Na+ currents were assessed using the whole-cell patch-clamp technique on cardiac myocytes isolated from WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. In all experiments, the series resistance was compensated by at least 70% and each protocol used a holding voltage of -100 mV.
###end p 63

###xml 1052 1058 1048 1054 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;7</xref>
###xml 1058 1059 1054 1055 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 1077 1078 1073 1074 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1118 1123 1114 1119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1123 1126 1119 1122 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1190 1191 1186 1187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1213 1218 1209 1214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1218 1221 1214 1217 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1232 1238 1228 1234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;7</xref>
###xml 1238 1239 1234 1235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 1266 1267 1262 1263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1283 1284 1279 1280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1300 1301 1296 1297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1321 1322 1317 1318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1433 1434 1429 1430 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
Firstly, Na+ current densities and voltage dependence of activation were assessed using a pulse protocol which applied depolarizing pulses of 20 ms duration, from a holding potential of -100 mV, to test potentials between -90 and 70 mV in 10 mV increments. Fig. 7A compares families of representative current traces obtained from WT (left panel) and Scn3b-/- (right panel) myocytes in response to voltage steps, between the test potentials of -100 to 30 mV. In all the WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes examined, the greatest magnitude of peak Na+ current density was observed at voltage steps to either -30 or -40 mV. However, the maximum value of the peak Na+ current density was significantly smaller in the Scn3b-/- myocytes, compared to that shown in WT myocytes (Fig. 7A). Thus, Fig. 7B demonstrates that the maximum value of the peak current density at -30 mV was significantly reduced by 30% in Scn3b-/- myocytes when compared to that shown in WT myocytes (90.4 +/- 4.3 pA/pF, n = 7 vs. 63.3 +/- 4.8 pA/pF, n = 7 each, P < 0.001; Table 8). Furthermore, Fig. 7C plots the peak Na+ current densities obtained from WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes against the corresponding test potentials. The peak Na+ current densities in Scn3b-/- myocytes (Fig. 7C, white triangles) at -30 (P < 0.001), -20 (P < 0.001), -10 (P < 0.001) and 0 mV (P < 0.05) were significantly smaller than the corresponding densities recorded in WT myocytes (black triangles, n = 7 each).
###end p 64

Secondly, to examine changes in the biophysics of the Na+ channel activation and inactivation properties were assessed in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. The activation function of Na+ channels (Fig. 8A, squares) in WT (black) and Scn3b-/- (white) myocytes was obtained by plotting the peak Na+ conductance (gNa) (peak gNa) values against Vm. Peak gNa values were calculated by the following formula;where INa was the peak current density, Vm was membrane voltage and the ENa was the reversal potential of Na+ ions. This was calculated from the intracellular and extracellular Na+ concentration as an assumed value of 42.6 mV. The peak gNa values obtained were normalized to the corresponding maximum peak gNa values.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 314 315 314 315 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 1090 1091 1082 1083 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1142 1143 1134 1135 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1156 1161 1148 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1161 1164 1153 1156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1274 1275 1266 1267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">V</italic>
###xml 1275 1278 1267 1270 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1/2</sub>
###xml 1331 1336 1323 1328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1336 1339 1328 1331 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1405 1406 1393 1394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1417 1418 1405 1406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
Thirdly, the voltage dependence of inactivation was assessed using pre-pulses of 500 ms duration. These pre-pulses were applied over a voltage range from -120 to -20 mV in 10 mV increments. A test pulse to -20 mV of duration of 10 ms immediately followed this. The resulting currents were normalized against the Na+ current recorded at the pre-pulse at -120 mV. The inactivation function (Fig. 8A, circles) in WT (black) and Scn3b-/- (white) myocytes was obtained by plotting the normalized currents against Vm. The continuous lines display the Boltzmann functions fitted to the activation and inactivation data. The data was used to obtain the half-maximal voltages (V1/2) and slope factor (k) values of both activation and inactivation in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes (Table 8). The activation function of the Na+ channel in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes remained similar, despite a smaller Na+ current recorded in Scn3b-/- myocytes. Thus, the V1/2 and k values of WT (-41.0 +/- 0.2 mV and 2.4 +/- 0.3 mV) were similar to those in Scn3b-/- hearts (-43.6 +/- 0.4 mV and 2.1 +/- 0.2 mV, n = 7 each, P > 0.05). However, the inactivation curve of the Na+ channels in Scn3b-/- myocytes was shifted in the negative direction relative to the corresponding curve in WT myocytes. Thus, the V1/2 in the voltage dependence of inactivation of WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes was -59.5 +/- 0.4 mV and -67.0 +/- 0.4 mV respectively (n = 7 each, P < 0.01).
###end p 66

###xml 290 291 286 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 392 397 388 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 397 400 393 396 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 491 496 487 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 496 499 492 495 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 624 629 620 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 629 632 625 628 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 793 798 789 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 798 801 794 797 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
However, the slope factors of the inactivation curves were similar in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes (WT; 5.7 +/- 0.3 mV vs. Scn3b-/-; 6.4 +/- 0.4 mV, n = 7 each, P > 0.05). At the holding potential of -100 mV, the normalized inactivation current was 0.95 in both WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes (Fig. 8A). However, at a depolarized potential of -80 mV, the normalized values were 0.93 and 0.84 in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes respectively. This suggests that at -80 mV, an additional 10% of the channels in Scn3b-/- myocytes were already inactivated, compared to those in WT myocytes. Furthermore, the percentage of inactivated channels in Scn3b-/- myocytes, compared to WT myocytes, increases to 37% at a potential of -70 mV. This was calculated from the normalized current values of 0.83 and 0.61 in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes respectively.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 521 524 521 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 541 544 539 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 607 613 603 609 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig8" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;8</xref>
###xml 613 614 609 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 616 623 612 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl8" ref-type="table">Table 8</xref>
###xml 710 713 706 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 758 759 748 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 768 773 758 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 773 776 763 766 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 812 813 798 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 819 820 805 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 833 836 819 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#964;</italic>
###xml 881 882 861 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 891 896 871 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 896 899 876 879 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 936 937 912 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 943 944 919 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 970 976 946 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="fig8" ref-type="fig">Fig.&#160;8</xref>
###xml 976 977 952 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
Finally, the time course of recovery from inactivation was examined using a 1 s pre-pulse to -20 mV. This was followed by a return to the holding voltage of -100 mV to allow recovery, at varying durations between 1 and 250 ms. A test pulse at a duration of 50 ms to -20 mV determined the current observed in fractions of recovered channels. The currents recorded were normalized against the current obtained from each of the 1 s pre-pulses applied. To determine the relative proportion of channels that were in the fast (tau-fast) and slow (tau-slow) phase, a 2-exponential function was fitted to the data (Fig. 8B, Table 8). No significant differences were observed in the time constants and fractions of the tau-fast (WT; 2.3 +/- 0.5 ms and 0.83 +/- 0.07, n = 7 vs. Scn3b-/-; 2.1 +/- 0.2 ms and 0.97 +/- 0.04, n = 7, P > 0.05) and tau-slow (WT; 27.1 +/- 7.5 ms and 0.3 +/- 0.05, n = 7 vs. Scn3b-/-; 39.5 +/- 5.3 ms and 0.27 +/- 0.02, n = 7, P > 0.05) values obtained (Fig. 8B).
###end p 68
###begin title 69
Discussion
###end title 69
###begin p 70
###xml 10 11 10 11 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 124 135 124 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib14" ref-type="bibr">Grant, 2001</xref>
###xml 161 166 161 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN5A</italic>
###xml 208 213 208 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 239 240 235 236 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 251 252 247 248 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 339 383 335 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib4 bib10" ref-type="bibr">Brugada and Brugada, 1992; Chen et&#160;al., 1998</xref>
###xml 416 433 412 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib51" ref-type="bibr">Wang et&#160;al., 1995</xref>
###xml 499 504 495 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 504 507 500 503 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 512 517 508 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 517 527 513 519 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
###xml 558 599 550 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib16 bib38" ref-type="bibr">Head et&#160;al., 2005; Papadatos et&#160;al., 2002</xref>
###xml 701 702 693 694 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 738 743 730 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KCNE1</italic>
###xml 771 820 763 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2 bib50" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003; Vetter et&#160;al., 1996</xref>
###xml 868 888 860 880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib23" ref-type="bibr">Killeen et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 529 535 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 602 608 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Murine</span>
Sodium (Na+) channel function is critical for normal initiation, conduction and propagation of cardiac electrical activity (Grant, 2001). Thus, mutations in the SCN5A gene, which encodes for the pore-forming alpha-subunit of the cardiac Na+ channel Nav1.5, result in clinical arrhythmic conditions that include the Brugada syndrome (BrS) (Brugada and Brugada, 1992; Chen et al., 1998) and long QT syndrome 3 (LQT3) (Wang et al., 1995). These conditions have been reproduced in genetically modified, Scn5a+/- and Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ, murine models, respectively (Head et al., 2005; Papadatos et al., 2002). Murine models have also been useful in studying the consequences of alterations in the potassium (K+) channel, such as mutations in the KCNE1 subunit resulting in LQT5 (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003; Vetter et al., 1996) and of acute conditions such as hypokalaemia (Killeen et al., 2007).
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 33 37 33 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 44 49 41 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 135 136 128 129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

###xml 198 203 188 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>

###xml 283 284 269 270 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 293 297 279 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>

###xml 358 359 338 339 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
