###xml 381 385 361 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 385 386 362 363 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 388 406 365 383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib19" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995a</xref>
###xml 409 413 386 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 413 414 387 388 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 416 435 390 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib35" ref-type="bibr">Morgan et&#160;al., 2000</xref>
###xml 441 445 415 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 445 446 416 417 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 457 472 428 443 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib54" ref-type="bibr">Yu et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 489 494 460 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN1B</italic>
###xml 496 501 467 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN2B</italic>
###xml 503 508 474 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN3B</italic>
###xml 513 518 484 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN4B</italic>
###xml 547 551 518 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 551 553 519 521 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1A</sub>
###xml 555 583 523 551 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib21" ref-type="bibr">Kazen-Gillespie et&#160;al., 2000</xref>
###xml 589 593 557 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 593 595 558 560 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1B</sub>
###xml 597 613 562 578 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib40" ref-type="bibr">Qin et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 660 665 625 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN1B</italic>
###xml 703 707 668 669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 707 708 669 670 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 710 714 672 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 714 715 673 674 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 717 721 676 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 721 722 677 678 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 727 731 683 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 731 732 684 685 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 819 840 772 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib5" ref-type="bibr">Candenas et&#160;al., 2006</xref>
###xml 862 957 815 910 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib20 bib30 bib35 bib40 bib54" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995b; Makita et&#160;al., 1994; Morgan et&#160;al., 2000; Qin et&#160;al., 2003; Yu et&#160;al., 2003</xref>
###xml 1050 1068 1003 1021 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib20" ref-type="bibr">Isom et&#160;al., 1995b</xref>
###xml 1127 1128 1080 1081 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1138 1219 1091 1172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib8 bib33 bib35 bib39" ref-type="bibr">Chen et&#160;al., 2002; Meadows et&#160;al., 2002; Morgan et&#160;al., 2000; Patton et&#160;al., 1994</xref>
###xml 1275 1279 1228 1229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1358 1359 1308 1309 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1424 1428 1374 1375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1428 1429 1375 1376 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1485 1486 1432 1433 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 1490 1495 1437 1438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#945;</italic>
###xml 1506 1522 1449 1465 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib24" ref-type="bibr">Kim et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 1556 1561 1499 1504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1561 1564 1504 1507 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1606 1611 1549 1554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1636 1663 1579 1606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib28" ref-type="bibr">Lopez-Santiago et&#160;al., 2007</xref>
###xml 1683 1687 1626 1627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 78 84 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 775 780 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
There have been fewer studies of beta- than alpha-subunits of ion channels in murine systems, particularly those associated with the Na+ channel. One or more of such beta-subunits associate with an alpha-subunit to form the complete channel (Catterall, 2000). So far, six types of Na+ channel beta-subunits have been identified and cloned. Of these, the beta1 (Isom et al., 1992), beta2 (Isom et al., 1995a), beta3 (Morgan et al., 2000) and beta4 subunits (Yu et al., 2003) are encoded by SCN1B, SCN2B, SCN3B and SCN4B respectively. The remaining beta1A (Kazen-Gillespie et al., 2000) and beta1B (Qin et al., 2003) subunits are generated by splice variants of SCN1B. mRNA transcripts encoding for these beta1, beta2, beta3 and beta4 subunits are expressed in a wide range of human tissues that include brain, skeletal (Candenas et al., 2006) and cardiac muscle (Isom et al., 1995b; Makita et al., 1994; Morgan et al., 2000; Qin et al., 2003; Yu et al., 2003). The expression of these subunits is thought to be important in normal surface expression (Isom et al., 1995b) and determining the biophysical characteristics of the Na+ channel (Chen et al., 2002; Meadows et al., 2002; Morgan et al., 2000; Patton et al., 1994). It has also been suggested that cleaved forms of the beta-subunits may act as transcription factors for mRNA transcripts encoding for Na+ channel subunits. Thus, the cleaved intracellular domain of the beta2 subunit has been shown to increase the expression of Nav1.1 alpha-subunits (Kim et al., 2007). Furthermore, the ventricles of Scn1b-/- hearts have greater expression levels of Scn5a mRNA than do WT hearts (Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007). Modifications in beta-subunits thus have potential effects on cardiac electrophysiology.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 56 61 56 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 150 151 150 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 214 219 214 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 219 222 219 222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 471 476 471 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 476 479 476 479 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 562 579 562 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib9" ref-type="bibr">Chen et&#160;al., 2004</xref>
###xml 694 699 694 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 715 720 715 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 720 723 720 723 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 834 839 834 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 844 849 844 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 907 912 907 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1084 1088 1084 1085 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1088 1089 1085 1086 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1163 1168 1160 1165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1168 1171 1165 1168 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1226 1273 1223 1270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib28 bib29" ref-type="bibr">Lopez-Santiago et&#160;al., 2007; Maier et&#160;al., 2004</xref>
###xml 1289 1294 1286 1291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1321 1326 1318 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1326 1329 1323 1326 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1352 1357 1349 1354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1362 1367 1359 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1388 1393 1385 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1393 1396 1390 1393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1470 1475 1467 1472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1566 1589 1563 1586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib32" ref-type="bibr">Marionneau et&#160;al., 2005</xref>
###xml 1601 1606 1598 1603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1646 1651 1643 1648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1651 1654 1648 1651 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1777 1782 1774 1779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1782 1785 1779 1782 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1803 1808 1800 1805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1879 1884 1876 1881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1884 1887 1881 1884 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1957 1962 1954 1959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1962 1965 1959 1962 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 72 78 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 223 227 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 313 317 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 416 420 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 480 484 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 858 864 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 1172 1177 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
We report, for the first time, that deficiencies in the Scn3b gene in a murine system lead to altered biochemical and biophysical properties of the Na+ channel, resulting in abnormal ventricular electrophysiology. Scn3b-/- mice were first created using homologous recombination in embryonic stem (ES) cells. Such mice showed no significant changes in behavioural and metabolic tests compared to those assessed in WT mice. These findings are in contrast to those shown in Scn1b-/- mice, which demonstrate ataxic gait, generalized seizures and growth retardation (Chen et al., 2004). Reverse-transcriptase polymerase chain reaction (RT-PCR) analysis not only confirmed the presence or absence of Scn3b mRNA in WT and Scn3b-/- hearts respectively, but also that the Scn3b mRNA or protein may exert a regulatory role on the expression of Scn1b and Scn5a mRNA in murine ventricles. Firstly, it demonstrated that Scn3b mRNA was expressed in wild-type (WT) with similar expression in both the left and right ventricles. This was in agreement with previous studies that had demonstrated that beta3 subunits were expressed in the ventricular myocytes obtained from WT and Scn1b-/- mouse hearts, specifically in the transverse tubules (Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007; Maier et al., 2004). As expected, Scn3b mRNA was not expressed in Scn3b-/- hearts. Secondly, the Scn1b and Scn5a mRNA in both WT and Scn3b-/- ventricles were expressed at higher levels compared to the expression of Scn3b mRNA in WT hearts, confirming a previous report concerning such experiments in WT hearts (Marionneau et al., 2005). Thirdly, Scn1b mRNA was expressed at higher levels in Scn3b-/- hearts than in WT hearts. These levels of expression were greater in the left than in the right ventricles in both WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. Finally, Scn5a mRNA was expressed at similar levels in the left ventricles of WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. It was expressed at higher levels in the right ventricles of Scn3b-/- hearts, compared to levels in the right ventricles of WT hearts.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 67 72 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 72 75 72 75 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 392 397 392 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 397 400 397 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 402 407 402 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 407 417 407 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
###xml 419 424 415 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kcne1</italic>
###xml 424 427 420 423 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 475 482 471 478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl9" ref-type="table">Table 9</xref>
###xml 584 677 580 673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib2 bib16 bib23 bib38" ref-type="bibr">Balasubramaniam et&#160;al., 2003; Head et&#160;al., 2005; Killeen et&#160;al., 2007; Papadatos et&#160;al., 2002</xref>
###xml 693 698 689 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 698 701 694 697 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 917 924 913 920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl9" ref-type="table">Table 9</xref>
###xml 954 959 950 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 959 962 955 958 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1090 1091 1086 1087 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1093 1094 1089 1090 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1157 1162 1153 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1162 1165 1158 1161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1406 1411 1402 1407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1411 1414 1407 1410 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1464 1466 1460 1462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1547 1552 1543 1548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 1552 1555 1548 1551 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1659 1661 1651 1653 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">90</sub>
###xml 1738 1743 1730 1735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 1743 1746 1735 1738 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 385 391 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 464 469 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 492 498 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 530 535 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1382 1388 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
Electrophysiological studies in the ventricles of the whole intact Scn3b-/- hearts also showed arrhythmogenesis and conduction abnormalities. This arrhythmogenesis took the form of either monomorphic or polymorphic ventricular tachycardias (VTs). These electrophysiological findings showed both similarities and contrasts to earlier results obtained from experiments on arrhythmogenic murine Scn5a+/-, Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ, Kcne1-/- and hypokalaemic hearts, as well as human BrS (Table 9(A)). The murine systems had been used to model human BrS, LQT3, LQT5 and hypokalaemia, respectively (Balasubramaniam et al., 2003; Head et al., 2005; Killeen et al., 2007; Papadatos et al., 2002). Firstly, the Scn3b-/- hearts showed VT during programmed electrical stimulation (PES) and paced electrogram fractionation analysis (PEFA) of these results demonstrated abnormal conduction curves, in common with the remaining examples in Table 9(A). These curves showed that Scn3b-/- hearts had electrogram duration (EGD) ratios that were significantly longer but conduction latencies that were similar at the S1-S2 interval of 125 ms as those shown in WT hearts. Secondly, the Scn3b-/- hearts showed shorter ventricular effective refractory periods (VERPs) than in WT hearts, in common with findings from hypokalaemic hearts and clinical cases of BrS but in contrast to features shown by the remaining murine models. Finally, Scn3b-/- hearts had shorter endocardial and epicardial APD90 values than did WT hearts. Nevertheless, the difference between these values in Scn3b-/- hearts, which offers a measure of the transmural gradient of repolarization in the form of the DeltaAPD90, was similar to that shown by WT hearts. This is in common with findings in Scn5a+/- hearts but in contrast to the remaining examples.
###end p 73

###xml 2416 2426 2372 2378 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
###xml 2535 2589 2487 2541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib15 bib42 bib53" ref-type="bibr">Guo et al., 1999; Remme et al., 2006; Yao et al., 1998</xref>
###xml 2670 2671 2622 2623 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2684 2689 2636 2641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 2689 2692 2641 2644 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2804 2809 2756 2761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 2809 2812 2761 2764 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2891 2896 2843 2848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 2896 2906 2848 2854 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#916;KPQ</sup>
The use of the whole-cell patch-clamp technique demonstrated the loss of function of the cardiac Na+ channel in ventricular myocytes isolated from Scn3b-/- hearts. These experiments were carried out at the same temperature of 37 degreesC as the studies used on intact hearts in contrast to previous investigations that had carried out similar single cell experiments at room temperature (Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007; Papadatos et al., 2002). Table 9(B) compares the resulting Na+ channel properties in Scn3b-/- myocytes with those shown in Scn5a+/- and Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ myocytes and points to a number of important comparisons. Firstly, Scn3b-/- myocytes showed significantly smaller peak Na+ current densities, in response to depolarizing voltage steps from a -100 mV holding potential, than did WT myocytes. This was in common with previous findings in Scn5a+/- myocytes but in contrast to those shown in Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ myocytes (Table 9(B)). This suggests a reduced expression or proportion of functional Na+ channels in the plasma membrane of Scn3b-/- ventricles compared to that shown in WT ventricles. The present experiments were performed under conditions of higher ratios of extracellular and intracellular [Na+]. This may account for the larger Na+ current densities observed in the present study, compared to those observed in previous investigations (Nuyens et al., 2001; Papadatos et al., 2002). Both latter studies used lower extracellular and intracellular [Na+] ratios of 2:1 and 2:2 respectively and carried out single cell experiments at room temperature (22-23 degreesC). Such conditions had resulted in peak Na+ current densities of approximately15 pA/pF and 21 +/- 5 pA/pF respectively. Secondly, the Na+ channel activation properties in Scn3b-/- myocytes were similar to those of WT myocytes in common with findings in Scn5a+/- and Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ myocytes. However, the present findings were obtained at a higher temperature of 37 degreesC than used in the previous studies (Lopez-Santiago et al., 2007; Papadatos et al., 2002). This may account for the similarly highly rapid time courses of activation and small slope factors of steady-state activation observed in both the WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. Thirdly, the position of the inactivation curves in Scn3b-/- myocytes was nevertheless shifted in the negative direction relative to that shown in WT myocytes, whereas both Scn5a+/- and Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ myocytes showed normal inactivation curves. At a typical resting membrane potential between -80 and -70 mV (Guo et al., 1999; Remme et al., 2006; Yao et al., 1998), such a shift would result in the inactivation of a further 10 to 37% of the Na+ channels in Scn3b-/- myocytes, compared to that shown in WT myocytes. Finally, the time course in the recovery from inactivation in Scn3b-/- myocytes were similar to that shown in WT myocytes in common with findings in Scn5a+/DeltaKPQ myocytes.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 29 30 29 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 82 87 82 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 87 90 87 90 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 145 152 145 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 155 156 155 156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 381 382 381 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 481 482 481 482 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 491 495 491 492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 570 575 567 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN1B</italic>
###xml 660 681 657 678 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib52" ref-type="bibr">Watanabe et&#160;al., 2008</xref>
###xml 843 844 840 841 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 953 954 950 951 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 974 978 971 972 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1024 1025 1018 1019 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1097 1098 1091 1092 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1190 1191 1184 1185 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 1202 1206 1196 1197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1303 1307 1294 1295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 1422 1450 1410 1438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib28" ref-type="bibr">Lopez-Santiago et&#160;al. (2007)</xref>
###xml 1480 1485 1468 1473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn1b</italic>
###xml 1537 1538 1525 1526 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 641 649 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 737 752 <span type="species:ncbi:10029">Chinese hamster</span>
###xml 1496 1502 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
Together, the altered peak Na+ current density and inactivation features shown in Scn3b-/- myocytes are compatible with a reduction of the total in vivo Na+ current. This is compatible with findings in BrS. Thus, although the clinical cases of BrS have shown a wide range of alterations in the activation, inactivation and recovery from inactivation properties, all show reduced Na+ currents. The present findings also add a further example of BrS that involves mutations in the Na+ channel beta-subunit. A previous investigation had identified a single mutation in the SCN1B gene and two mutations in the splice variant of the same gene in patients with BrS (Watanabe et al., 2008). It used a heterologous expression system provided by Chinese hamster ovary (CHO) cells, to study the consequent changes in the biophysical properties of the Na+ channel resulting from the mutations. In agreement with the present example, cells expressing both the WT Nav1.5 and such mutant beta-subunits showed significantly reduced peak Na+ currents. In contrast, activation and inactivation properties of the Na+ channel shifted in the positive direction in relation to findings in cells expressing WT Nav1.5 and WT beta-subunits. The present findings also complement other investigations in which alterations in the beta-subunit expression can produce other electrophysiological changes that include a LQT-like phenotype. For example, Lopez-Santiago et al. (2007) associated a deletion of the Scn1b gene in a murine system with an increase in peak Na+ currents and QT prolongation.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 53 54 53 54 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 101 105 101 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 105 106 102 103 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 206 213 203 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 247 255 244 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 315 322 312 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 524 525 521 522 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 534 541 531 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 543 564 540 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib1" ref-type="bibr">Abriel and Kass, 2005</xref>
###xml 590 597 587 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xenopus</italic>
###xml 631 632 628 629 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 640 644 637 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 644 645 638 639 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 696 697 690 691 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 781 782 775 776 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 792 810 786 804 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib12" ref-type="bibr">Fahmi et&#160;al., 2001</xref>
###xml 849 850 843 844 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 858 862 852 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
###xml 862 863 853 854 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 900 901 891 892 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1005 1006 996 997 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</sub>
###xml 1016 1031 1007 1022 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="bib26" ref-type="bibr">Ko et&#160;al., 2005</xref>
###xml 590 597 <span type="species:ncbi:8355">Xenopus</span>
The present findings complement reports of altered Na+ channel biophysical properties resulting from beta3 expression in heterologous expression systems by describing the consequences of similar expression in vivo. However, the properties of such in vitro expression systems may not correspond to features observed in vivo and have demonstrated conflicting results despite the transfection of identical sets of genes. Such systems lack functionally important proteins such as ankyrin proteins that form complexes with the Na+ channel in vivo (Abriel and Kass, 2005). Thus, on the one hand, Xenopus oocytes injected with cRNA for Nav1.5 and beta3 subunits demonstrated significantly larger peak Na+ currents and positive shifts in the inactivation curves than in cells expressing Nav1.5 only (Fahmi et al., 2001). In contrast, CHO cells expressing Nav1.5 and beta3 subunits resulted in similar peak Na+ currents with negative shifts in the activation and inactivation curves compared to cells expressing Nav1.5 only (Ko et al., 2005).
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 69 74 69 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 187 192 187 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn5a</italic>
###xml 192 195 192 195 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
In conclusion, we have for the first time associated the lack of the Scn3b gene with a ventricular arrhythmogenesis in intact perfused hearts whose features are similar to those shown in Scn5a+/- hearts.
###end p 77

###begin p 149
###xml 25 30 25 30 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 38 39 38 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 73 78 73 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 170 175 170 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn3b</italic>
###xml 220 223 220 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Afl</italic>
###xml 227 228 227 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</italic>
###xml 234 237 234 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bcl</italic>
###xml 240 241 240 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 626 627 623 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</italic>
###xml 703 706 700 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Afl</italic>

###xml 504 508 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Targeted deletion of the Scn3b gene. (A) Schematic representation of the Scn3b allele that was targeted for deletion. The top line shows a partial restriction map of the Scn3b locus, indicating the restriction sites for AflII (A) and BclI (B). The centre line represents the targeted vector and the predicted targeted allele after homologous recombination shown in the bottom line. The location of the PCR primers and the probe used for screening the correctly targeted embryonic stem (ES) cells and the mice are shown. IRES; internal ribosome entry site, beta-gal; beta-galactosidase gene and Neo; neomycin resistance gene. (B) Southern blot analysis of a successfully targeted ES cell. Digestion with AflII yielded a 7.7 kb endogenous band and a 12.6 kb bp targeted band as predicted. Digestion with BclI resulted in a 7.2 kb endogenous band and the predicted 7.8 kb bp targeted band. (C) PCR analysis identified band sizes of 204 bp in the wild-type (+/+) allele and 334 bp in homozygote knockout (-/-) allele. Both bands were observed in the heterozygote (+/-) allele. A water control was used to assess the specificity of the primers used. All 5 lanes shown were obtained from the same gel.

RT-PCR analysis of mRNA expression. The relative abundance of mRNA (normalized and calculated as % of GAPDH expression) of encoding Na+ channel subunit transcripts. Electrogram waveforms and conduction curves from programmed electrical stimulation (PES) and bipolar electrogram (BEG) recordings. The electrograms recorded at the longest S1-S2 interval (basic cycle length of 125 ms) in WT hearts (A) were significantly shorter in duration than in Scn3b-/- hearts (C). Similarly, electrograms obtained prior to the heart becoming refractory or arrhythmic were consistently shorter in duration in WT hearts (B) than those recorded in Scn3b-/- hearts (D). (E) Conduction curves were created by the application of paced electrogram fractionation analysis (PEFA) to PES data obtained from WT (white circles) and Scn3b-/- hearts (black circles). The vertical axis represents latency (ms) and the horizontal axis, the S1-S2 interval (ms). The representative conduction curve demonstrates a greater increase in electrogram duration at the shortest S1-S2 interval and shorter VERP in Scn3b-/- hearts, than recorded in WT hearts.

Peak Na+ current densities in WT and Scn3b-/- myocytes. Representative Na+ current traces recorded from WT (A, left panel) and Scn3b-/- (A, right panel) myocytes. (B) The peak Na+ current densities were significantly smaller in Scn3b-/- myocytes (white column, n = 7) compared to those shown in WT myocytes (black column, n = 7). (C) The current-voltage relationship demonstrated a smaller Na+ current in Scn3b-/- myocytes (white triangles, n = 7) between the voltage steps of -30 and 0 mV compared to those shown in WT myocytes (black triangles, n = 7). *P < 0.05, ***P < 0.001. All recordings were obtained at 37 degreesC.
###end p 155

###xml 810 817 810 817 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" rid="tbl8" ref-type="table">Table 8</xref>
###xml 820 821 820 821 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 832 833 832 833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 845 846 845 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
Steady-state activation, inactivation and recovery from inactivation properties in WT and Scn3b-/- hearts. (A) Steady-state voltage dependence of activation (square symbols) and inactivation (circle symbols) in WT (black symbols) and Scn3b-/- (white symbols) myocytes. The solid lines represent the Boltzmann fits. The normalized inactivation currents were significantly smaller in Scn3b-/- myocytes (n = 7) between the voltage steps of -70 and -40 mV compared to those shown in WT myocytes (n = 7). The pulse protocols used to study the voltage dependence of activation and inactivation are shown in the inset. (B) Recovery from inactivation in WT (black diamonds) and Scn3b-/- (white diamonds) myocytes. The solid lines represent double-exponential fits. The derived biophysical properties are summarised in Table 8. *P < 0.05, **P < 0.01, ***P < 0.001. All recordings were obtained at 37 degreesC.
